  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_485a6622-cb13-4ff9-82d3-4a2fdf341c9f'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9390876196126092446">Dean Koontz's unique talent for writing terrifying thrillers with a heart and soul is nowhere more evident than in this latest suspense masterpiece that pits one man against the ultimate deadline. If there were speed limits for the sheer pulse-racing excitement allowed in one novel, "Velocity" would break them all. Get ready for the ride of your life. <br/><br/>Bill Wiles is an easy</span>
  <span id="freeText9390876196126092446" style="display:none">Dean Koontz's unique talent for writing terrifying thrillers with a heart and soul is nowhere more evident than in this latest suspense masterpiece that pits one man against the ultimate deadline. If there were speed limits for the sheer pulse-racing excitement allowed in one novel, "Velocity" would break them all. Get ready for the ride of your life. <br /><br />Bill Wiles is an easygoing, hardworking guy who leads a quiet, ordinary life. But that is about to change. One evening, after his usual eight-hour bartending shift, he finds a typewritten note under the windshield wiper of his car. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"If you don't take this note to the police and get them involved, I will kill a lovely blond schoolteacher. If you do take this note to the police, I will instead kill an elderly woman active in charity work. You have four hours to decide. The choice is yours."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />It seems like a sick joke, and Bill's friend on the police force, Lanny Olson, thinks so too. His advice to Bill is to go home and forget about it. Besides, what could they do even if they took the note seriously? No crime has actually been committed. But less than twenty-four hours later, a young blond schoolteacher is found murdered, and it's Bill's fault: he didn't convince the police to get involved. Now he's got another note, another deadline, another ultimatum...and two new lives hanging in the balance. <br /><br />Suddenly Bill's average, seemingly innocuous life takes on the dimensions and speed of an accelerating nightmare. Because the notes are coming faster, the deadlines growing tighter, and the killer becoming bolder and crueler with every communication--until Bill is isolated with the terrifying knowledge that he alone has the power of life and death over a psychopath's innocent victims. Until the struggle between good and evil is intensely personal. Until the most chilling words of all are: <i>"The choice is yours."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9390876196126092446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1139923374" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1139923374" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1139923374?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1139923374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8599939282157394329">A very weak novel by Koontz. it's like he was contradicting himself when he gave the book a title of "Velocity" when in reality it was slow as shit. <br/><br/>The main character was really likable at first, but he slowly became boring as the novel went by. I didn't seem to hold my interest because most of the book contained nothing but jibber jabber. A lot of useless stuff written just for the novel to be longer than it should be. The amount of useless things said over powered the little of action that th</span>
  <span id="freeText8599939282157394329" style="display:none">A very weak novel by Koontz. it's like he was contradicting himself when he gave the book a title of "Velocity" when in reality it was slow as shit. <br /><br />The main character was really likable at first, but he slowly became boring as the novel went by. I didn't seem to hold my interest because most of the book contained nothing but jibber jabber. A lot of useless stuff written just for the novel to be longer than it should be. The amount of useless things said over powered the little of action that the novel had. <br /><br />The plot had huge potential, but the jibber jabber really destroyed it. A supposed suspenseful novel turned into a sleep inducing one. It took me forever to finish this (almost a month) and that means that I really wasn't interested. I finished it just for the sake of it, and because I really hate to DNF a book. I haven't really seen the truth in "If you like Stephen King, then try Dean Koontz" just yet, but maybe some of his other better novels would make me realize the implication.<br /><br />1.5/5 stars. I'm sure that I didn't pick up the wrong Koontz novel based on the synopsis, because that shit was good and exciting. It's also not because I wasn't in the mood for such genre, because I was. The book was just terrible for me, let's leave it at that. Nothing works for everybody anyway. Once again, I'm still not giving up on Koontz, because his Odd Thomas novels were quite entertaining anyway(at least the ones I've currently read). Read at your own risk.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8599939282157394329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer347122329792740751"><b>
  <u>This is indeed a novel with speed incorporated!</u>
</b><br/><br/>As the title <i>Velocity</i> hints the rhythm of the narrative. A clear fast tempo.<br/><br/>You are barely getting comfy in your seat when you realize that you need to fasten your seatbelt right away!<br/><br/>The premise is simple but performed in a brilliant and very entertaining way.<br/><br/>I liked real quick the protagonist and I fear even quicker from the antagonist. <br/><br/>Nothing is left to the chance.   <span id="freeText347122329792740751" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>This is indeed a novel with speed incorporated!</u>
</b><br /><br />As the title <i>Velocity</i> hints the rhythm of the narrative. A clear fast tempo.<br /><br />You are barely getting comfy in your seat when you realize that you need to fasten your seatbelt right away!<br /><br />The premise is simple but performed in a brilliant and very entertaining way.<br /><br />I liked real quick the protagonist and I fear even quicker from the antagonist. <br /><br />Nothing is left to the chance. You will witness a carefull crafted masterful plan by the villain.<br /><br />I enjoyed in the way that story develops since you realize that the protagonist takes sound and reasonable decisions at each moment that he/she needs to take a choice. It's not like "Oh, for Christ's sake! Why in the world he is doing that?! He/she drives me nuts!" Oh, no, no. I think that the protagonist reacts in a very believable way.<br /><br />Moreover, the story is totally set in a real world ambiance, you won't met any paranormal force.<br /><br />The evil here is very real and truly scary with a flesh-and-blood psychopathic criminal.<br /><br />Also, since it's a very entertaining story and real page-turner, you will read it real quick.<br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="347122329792740751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_11729733" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11729733" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/733629-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199331851p2/733629.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11729733?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/733629-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11729733" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13053295099720059391">Usually people go on smoke breaks at work to take a break from their routine paper-pushing to talk all raw about chicks and cuss a lot. Thank god where I work I can do these things from the comfort of my desk, so when I go on a smoke break I can talk about things that actually take up to ten minutes to discuss (seeing as I’ve been seeing the same chick for years I don’t have much in the way of interesting conversation anyway). Sometimes I will rap about the futility of Chicago football, usually </span>
  <span id="freeText13053295099720059391" style="display:none">Usually people go on smoke breaks at work to take a break from their routine paper-pushing to talk all raw about chicks and cuss a lot. Thank god where I work I can do these things from the comfort of my desk, so when I go on a smoke break I can talk about things that actually take up to ten minutes to discuss (seeing as I’ve been seeing the same chick for years I don’t have much in the way of interesting conversation anyway). Sometimes I will rap about the futility of Chicago football, usually I’m rapping in a negative manner about the clods I have to deal with in a day’s work, or sometimes movies and music, and once in a great while, I’ll actually discuss a book. Usually it’s just one person talking about the book and how much it ruled or sucked while the other person nods with slight enthusiasm; this is because finding two people who have read the same book and can openly discuss it in this day and age is less common than finding a large chunk of platinum sticking out of the ground. Well, even if you’re not on quite the same page, or in the same book, for that matter, you can get a recommendation of worth.<br /><br />	Or, you can be led into the fallacy that Dean Koontz is worth a shit as an author. Sure, someone might say ‘hey, if you like Stephen King you’ll love this guy’, and in the seldom-used recesses of the mind you think, ‘hmmm, I’ve been seeing Koontz’s name for ages, he’s obviously a NY Times bestseller several times over, maybe it’s time to finally give the guy a chance.<br /><br />	And Velocity is exactly the type of reason that I’m not listening to anyone tell me that a particular author is worth a damn. I’ll go back to either judging books by their cover or getting some recommendations from ‘Brick’, the spirit I channel via my ouija board. About all I can say on a positive note about this book is that I wasn’t exactly offended by it, not as if that is a rave review, but nothing within made me throw it out the window, a fate that’s been suffered by only two books in my time. It just doesn’t do anything for me; no entertainment, no enlightenment, it certainly didn’t make my manhood any bigger. <br /><br />Good old Billy, the common Everyman, becomes a pawn in a dangerous game being perpetrated by a crafty villain with the singular goal of psychologically harassing him while offing people. The catch; prior to every murder, the killer leaves Billy a note giving him two choices, either take no action and he’ll kill victim A or to run to the cops and he’ll kill victim B. As the game plods along, he starts including people who are close to Billy (or at least could be people close to him, as the descriptions of the victims are always vague enough not to point to anyone in particular) as potential victims, and our intrepid bartender has to use every shred of cunning and resourcefulness he can muster to rise to the challenge; to reveal the identity of this vicious bastard and kick his ass. The killer, of course, isn’t about to let him do that, and begins planting evidence on Billy’s property, pestering him over the phone, dropping misleading clues as to his identity, and generally being a nuisance. After the killer makes a few personal appearances and beats Billy down and becomes and even bigger pain in the ass, the final confrontation is afoot, in what might be the most mundane and completely preposterous finale imaginable. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13053295099720059391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_123669930" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123669930" />
    <a title="Maciek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek"><img alt="Maciek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280839159p2/2969647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123669930?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maciek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maciek" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek">Maciek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007196975" href="/book/show/906900.Velocity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=thriller-mystery-suspense">thriller-mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=own-in-paperback">own-in-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123669930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1851855543779801582"><i>Velocity</i> is the essence of mass-market fiction. Billy Wiles, an everyman bartender finds a note under the windshield of his car - If he takes it to the police, a schoolteacher will die. If he doesn't, an old woman will be killed. Billy visits his cop friend and tells him about the note. The cop thinks it's a hoax and tells Billy to dismiss it. It turns out it's not - the schoolteacher dies. Billy starts receiving other notes, forcing our bartender to choose the fate of people that are close to h</span>
  <span id="freeText1851855543779801582" style="display:none"><i>Velocity</i> is the essence of mass-market fiction. Billy Wiles, an everyman bartender finds a note under the windshield of his car - If he takes it to the police, a schoolteacher will die. If he doesn't, an old woman will be killed. Billy visits his cop friend and tells him about the note. The cop thinks it's a hoax and tells Billy to dismiss it. It turns out it's not - the schoolteacher dies. Billy starts receiving other notes, forcing our bartender to choose the fate of people that are close to him.<br /><br /><i>Velocity</i> moves along nicely and is fairly suspenseful until its faults start to kick in. In one scene the cops drive over to Billy because he mistakenly called 911. They grill him and even search his house. In another scene the cops give Billy details of a classified investigation over the phone without bothering to check who's calling (caller ID is enough).<br />Also another flaw is Koontz's limited knowledge of personal computers. Billy is worried about somebody checking his internet activities at the library computer because it could have a <i>keylogger</i>. Hasn't he heard about browsing history?<br />The biggest plot hole of all deal with disposing dead bodies. As Billy has to do something with quite a few of them, where does he go? You got it, to the Giant And Deep Hole No One Knows About. Several times. It's a deep lava vent hole that goes hundreds of feet down (it's essentially bottomless) and is conveniently located in his friend's backyard, so Billy doesn't even have to do much driving. Of course everything is nicely solved in an epilogue, because it's a Koontz novel and the good guy doesn't have to face the consequence of his actions.<br /><br />All the action is interrupted by dialogues, which are thinly veiled Koontz's personal ideas about things like modern art, universities and scientists, and Billy's deep, philosophical thoughts about himself, painkillers, and the world in general - they must sound profound, but not be too complicated for the average bored housewife to understand. It seems to me that Koontz has found his niche - or rather a whole shelf at the nearest Wall-Mart. Because that's what it is, folks - the Wall-Mart of fiction. Quoting T.S. Eliot and Hemingway does not make a book smart. There are shades of a good moments in <i>Velocity</i>, but the whole book will evaporate from your mind quickier than a dead body goes down that damn hole. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1851855543779801582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_228608390" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228608390" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6014887-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389632385p2/6014887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228608390?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/6014887-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007196975" href="/book/show/906900.Velocity">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Richard by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2393603-stephen-hegedus">Stephen Hegedus</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=recs-by-friends">recs-by-friends</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228608390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5264242942826709556">This is the first Dean Koontz novel I have ever read. I had thought of him as a sort of lesser version of Stephen King--pulpy and popular. While there was that in this novel, it was well crafted. The protagonist, Billy Wiles, proved to be a complex character. The identity of the villain was kept secret until close to the end. And there were literary allusions sprinkled throughout the book, which was a refreshing surprise. <br/><br/>The final scene seemed a little facile, and the villain seemed a little to</span>
  <span id="freeText5264242942826709556" style="display:none">This is the first Dean Koontz novel I have ever read. I had thought of him as a sort of lesser version of Stephen King--pulpy and popular. While there was that in this novel, it was well crafted. The protagonist, Billy Wiles, proved to be a complex character. The identity of the villain was kept secret until close to the end. And there were literary allusions sprinkled throughout the book, which was a refreshing surprise. <br /><br />The final scene seemed a little facile, and the villain seemed a little too much like a character out of a James Bond film. However, this did not detract too much from my enjoyment. The book was suspenseful and gripping. The title reflected not only important elements of the story, but also the pace at which I read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5264242942826709556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16788773660497594697">“A fine line separates the weary recluse from the fearful hermit. Finer still is the line between hermit and bitter misanthrope.” <br/>― Dean Koontz, Velocity<br/><br/><br/><br/>Imagine if you were to go to your car and had a note waiting for you in the way that Billy did. What on earth would you do?<br/><br/>I must say I have not read much of Koontz work. I did enjoy this fast paced little mystery though. The person who gave this novel to me said she had a tough time getting into it but I didn't. The beginning starts powerfully </span>
  <span id="freeText16788773660497594697" style="display:none">“A fine line separates the weary recluse from the fearful hermit. Finer still is the line between hermit and bitter misanthrope.” <br />― Dean Koontz, Velocity<br /><br /><br /><br />Imagine if you were to go to your car and had a note waiting for you in the way that Billy did. What on earth would you do?<br /><br />I must say I have not read much of Koontz work. I did enjoy this fast paced little mystery though. The person who gave this novel to me said she had a tough time getting into it but I didn't. The beginning starts powerfully and I was drawn right in.<br /><br />SPOILERS:<br /><br />I'd like to say the whole book was as good as the beginning but it wasn't. It was still worth reading, particularly if you like a good mystery.<br /><br />I enjoyed most of Velocity. The issue for me was the ending.<br /><br />There are also not alot of suspects in our pool to choose from. It is pretty easy to figure out who did it. The ending seemed overly dramatic when Billy is fighting the villain and I caught myself rolling my eyes a few times.<br /><br />What I liked best..surprisingly..was the very unusual love story. That is not the main focus of the story but it is in a way(if that makes any sense.). I found Billy's devotion to his girl to be quite touching and the book is worth reading just for that.<br /><br />3.5 stars. I enjoyed Velocity.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28067172-claudiu?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28067172-claudiu?shelf=politiste">politiste</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1944992145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11600973635880461609">If you are an avid reader of thrillers, you are instantly hooked when you read the backcover of Dean Koontz's novels written between 1995 - 2010. The bad thing about his novels is that the premises are very good. but the novels lack execution. <br/><br/>This is also the case of this 2005 novel called Velocity (translated into Romanian by Liviu Radu - a good translation) where the premise is very entertaining and it could have made a solid thriller if Koontz wouldn't have mixed genres and if he would have </span>
  <span id="freeText11600973635880461609" style="display:none">If you are an avid reader of thrillers, you are instantly hooked when you read the backcover of Dean Koontz's novels written between 1995 - 2010. The bad thing about his novels is that the premises are very good. but the novels lack execution. <br /><br />This is also the case of this 2005 novel called Velocity (translated into Romanian by Liviu Radu - a good translation) where the premise is very entertaining and it could have made a solid thriller if Koontz wouldn't have mixed genres and if he would have paid more attention to "small and irrevelant" details such as what is the motivation of the antagonist or how are clues being given to the protagonist. The ending felt a bit rushed. <br /><br />All in all, this a good read, good and entertaining, but I still feel kinda disappointed that Koontz hasn't offered more and that the hasn't played more with the potential of his premise (a premise which shows an author with a solid imagination).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11600973635880461609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10702780?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Sammis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Sammis" href="/user/show/122647-sarah-sammis">Sarah Sammis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=released">released</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/122647-sarah-sammis?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10702780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4272198568322127655">Velocity starts with death by garden gnome and gets weirder from there.<br/><br/>The back of the book has the message: "If you don’t take this note to the police and get them involved, I will kill a lovely blond schoolteacher. If you do take this note to the police, I will instead kill an elderly woman active in charity work. You have four hours to decide. The choice is yours." Going on that piece of information alone, one might think that Velocity will be a typical "ticking time bomb" type thriller; it i</span>
  <span id="freeText4272198568322127655" style="display:none">Velocity starts with death by garden gnome and gets weirder from there.<br /><br />The back of the book has the message: "If you don’t take this note to the police and get them involved, I will kill a lovely blond schoolteacher. If you do take this note to the police, I will instead kill an elderly woman active in charity work. You have four hours to decide. The choice is yours." Going on that piece of information alone, one might think that Velocity will be a typical "ticking time bomb" type thriller; it isn't.<br /><br />Bill Wile is more of an antihero than protagonist. He wants nothing to do with this secret person taunting him and framing him for murders. Because of his own shady past he doesn't feel comfortable going to the police even though he wants to.<br /><br />For observant readers, Koontz leaves lots of clues. They are hidden in plain sight. This is not a connect the dots mystery but one a second reading, the clues are there, popping out from the most unexpected places. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4272198568322127655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer890041488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13425302953151029377">I read a lot of Dean Koontz books in my teenage years. His writing style is very easy to adapt to and the stories are usually fast paced and fun. I have found that his books can be hit or miss...I loved some and couldn't finish others. Velocity ranks as one of my favorites by Koontz.<br/><br/>The Good: The author wastes no time in getting the story started. The reader is emerged in the action and adventure from the first chapter. The game of cat and mouse that is played between Billy and the unknown kille</span>
  <span id="freeText13425302953151029377" style="display:none">I read a lot of Dean Koontz books in my teenage years. His writing style is very easy to adapt to and the stories are usually fast paced and fun. I have found that his books can be hit or miss...I loved some and couldn't finish others. Velocity ranks as one of my favorites by Koontz.<br /><br />The Good: The author wastes no time in getting the story started. The reader is emerged in the action and adventure from the first chapter. The game of cat and mouse that is played between Billy and the unknown killer was a lot of fun and caused me to question what I would do in that situation. There were several twists that kept the story surprising and fresh. The book has many short chapters, which I prefer over few long chapters...it was a very quick read.<br /><br />What I didn't Like: Towards the end of the book, things became a bit monotonous and slightly predictable. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13425302953151029377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14150703265260106119">Billy Wiles is a bartender in a Napa Valley lounge.<br/>He works the day shift from around 11:00 a.m. until shortly after 6:00 p.m. helping the night shift barkeep during the 4-6 rush hour.<br/>It's a nice, peaceful bar. No troublemakers. No hassles. No drama. <br/><br/>One night Billy goes out to his Explorer and finds what appears to be a handbill underneath his windshield wiper-blade.<br/>He unfolds the neatly folded sheet of paper and finds the following:<br/><p>
  <b><br/>If you don't take this note to the police and get them invo</b></p></span>
  <span id="freeText14150703265260106119" style="display:none">Billy Wiles is a bartender in a Napa Valley lounge.<br />He works the day shift from around 11:00 a.m. until shortly after 6:00 p.m. helping the night shift barkeep during the 4-6 rush hour.<br />It's a nice, peaceful bar. No troublemakers. No hassles. No drama. <br /><br />One night Billy goes out to his Explorer and finds what appears to be a handbill underneath his windshield wiper-blade.<br />He unfolds the neatly folded sheet of paper and finds the following:<br /><p>
  <b><br />If you don't take this note to the police and get them involved, I will kill a lovely blond schoolteacher somewhere in Napa County.<br /><br />If you do take this note to the police, I will instead kill an elderly woman active in charity work.<br /><br />You have six hours to decide.<br />The choice is yours.<br /></b>
</p><br /><br />His immediate assumption is that the note is some kind of sick joke played upon him by one of his co-workers but the next afternoon he reads in the local newspaper an account of an unsolved murder of a school teacher that occurred overnight.<br /><br />The next night, he finds another taunting note.<br />The terror begins.<br /><br />This is an amazing read.<br />Riveting.<br />Terrifying.<br />As fast-paced as a Bruno Fischer hardboiled-thriller.<br />I'm in a state of awe.<br /><br />I held little regard for Dean Koontz prior to reading this thinking he was another prolific hack whose books were churned out like chocolate Easter rabbits at the candy factory.<br />I feel like such a judgemental jackass.<br />Frequently come across his books in used paperback shops and at library sales.<br />I'll no longer allow the opportunity to pick up on additional titles by Dean Koontz pass.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553804157" href="/book/show/437127.Velocity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=action-thriller">action-thriller</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer500811013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8062579782588720073">Maybe only 3.5 stars<br/><br/>This book was a bit of a misnomer for me. I thought the beginning was unique, intense, dripping with dark humor, and full of cliffhangers. At that point, each chapter added more and more to the speed of the story as the velocity increased and Billy's life quickly careened off course.<br/><br/>Then, about halfway through, the breaks were thrown on. Gone were the cliffhangers. The shorter, more intense chapters became interspersed with longer, more introspective chapters as Billy came cl</span>
  <span id="freeText8062579782588720073" style="display:none">Maybe only 3.5 stars<br /><br />This book was a bit of a misnomer for me. I thought the beginning was unique, intense, dripping with dark humor, and full of cliffhangers. At that point, each chapter added more and more to the speed of the story as the velocity increased and Billy's life quickly careened off course.<br /><br />Then, about halfway through, the breaks were thrown on. Gone were the cliffhangers. The shorter, more intense chapters became interspersed with longer, more introspective chapters as Billy came closer to determining the identity of the killer. And, while I don't have issue with longer, deeper chapters helping uncover parts of the plot, they just seemed to distract from the idea of "velocity"<br /><br />Finally, when the book was over, I couldn't really tell it was over. I was just waiting for a little bit more to happen. One more "SURPRISE!"<br /><br />But, despite my concerns with the book, I did enjoy it and would recommend it to other Koontz fans.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8062579782588720073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7047071-jo-ann?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7047071-jo-ann?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7047071-jo-ann?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7047071-jo-ann?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7047071-jo-ann?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7047071-jo-ann?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1218118167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10913630866549920363">This is only my second Koontz, and it was a big upgrade from my first experience with this author. Velocity is an appropriately named title for this quick read. This is one of those edge of your seat experiences. I'm usually pretty good at guessing who the villain is, but Koontz managed to keep me in suspense till almost the very end. I half guessed correctly, but I didn't see the second punch coming. Way to go Mr. Koontz! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_558029728" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Holly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1109907-holly"><img alt="Holly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208986867p2/1109907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20822809?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly" href="/user/show/1109907-holly">Holly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">who like fast pased murder mysteries</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Holly by: </span>
      DJ CC
  </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20822809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18041588116943431339">Dean Koontz’s unique talent for writing terrifying thrillers with a heart and soul is nowhere more evident than in this latest suspense masterpiece that pits one man against the ultimate deadline. If there were speed limits for the sheer pulse-racing excitement allowed in one novel, Velocity would break them all. Get ready for the ride of your life.<br/><br/>Velocity<br/><br/>Bill Wile is an easygoing, hardworking guy who leads a quiet, ordinary life. But that is about to change. One evening, after his usual eight-</span>
  <span id="freeText18041588116943431339" style="display:none">Dean Koontz’s unique talent for writing terrifying thrillers with a heart and soul is nowhere more evident than in this latest suspense masterpiece that pits one man against the ultimate deadline. If there were speed limits for the sheer pulse-racing excitement allowed in one novel, Velocity would break them all. Get ready for the ride of your life.<br /><br />Velocity<br /><br />Bill Wile is an easygoing, hardworking guy who leads a quiet, ordinary life. But that is about to change. One evening, after his usual eight-hour bartending shift, he finds a typewritten note under the windshield wiper of his car. If you don’t take this note to the police and get them involved, I will kill a lovely blond schoolteacher. If you do take this note to the police, I will instead kill an elderly woman active in charity work. You have four hours to decide. The choice is yours.<br /><br />It seems like a sick joke, and Bill’s friend on the police force, Lanny Olson, thinks so too. His advice to Bill is to go home and forget about it. Besides, what could they do even if they took the note seriously? No crime has actually been committed. But less than twenty-four hours later, a young blond schoolteacher is found murdered, and it’s Bill’s fault: he didn’t convince the police to get involved. Now he’s got another note, another deadline, another ultimatum…and two new lives hanging in the balance.<br /><br />Suddenly Bill’s average, seemingly innocuous life takes on the dimensions and speed of an accelerating nightmare. Because the notes are coming faster, the deadlines growing tighter, and the killer becoming bolder and crueler with every communication—until Bill is isolated with the terrifying knowledge that he alone has the power of life and death over a psychopath’s innocent victims. Until the struggle between good and evil is intensely personal. Until the most chilling words of all are: The choice is yours. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18041588116943431339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer4027113140407465308">Velocity by Dean Koontz<br/>	Napa County California seems to be a quiet place were not much really happens but things change when Billy Whiles gets off work at the local bar and finds a note under his windshield stating "If you don't take this note to the police and get them involved, I will kill a lovely blond schoolteacher. If you do take this note to the police, I will instead kill an elderly woman active in charity work. You have four hours to decide. The choice is yours." Billy takes the note to</span>
  <span id="freeText4027113140407465308" style="display:none">Velocity by Dean Koontz<br />	Napa County California seems to be a quiet place were not much really happens but things change when Billy Whiles gets off work at the local bar and finds a note under his windshield stating "If you don't take this note to the police and get them involved, I will kill a lovely blond schoolteacher. If you do take this note to the police, I will instead kill an elderly woman active in charity work. You have four hours to decide. The choice is yours." Billy takes the note to a friend; police officer named Lanny Olsen who dismisses the note as a sick joke. However the next day a lovely bond school teacher shows up dead in Napa County. Soon Billy begins to receive more notes giving him similar decisions and his quite life is turned upside down.<br />	Billy Whiles is a lonely bartender whose bride-to-be, Barbra, went into a coma four years earlier. He doesn’t have any close friends and passes his time doing wood work. He was previously an author however; when Barbra went into a coma he lost interest.<br />	The theme of the story is that things can change at any moment. Billy lived a quiet life but things defiantly changed when he started getting the notes. He quickly went from one of the more quiet laid back people in Napa County to someone being antagonized by a serial killer, and even drawn to kill……again.<br />	Velocity is defiantly a great action-adventure/suspense novel. It captivates and will always leave you wondering what will be around the next corner. Velocity is with out a doubt one of the best books I have ever read. Dean Koontz has defiantly created another masterpiece.<br />	<br /></span>

<div id="review_67270663" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67270663" />
    <a title="Troy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/600272-troy"><img alt="Troy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/67270663?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Troy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Troy" href="/user/show/600272-troy">Troy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67270663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5847798124709321968"><i>Velocity</i> certainly interested me enough to encourage quick reading, so the skeleton of the story can't be that bad. But I can only give it the two-star "it's okay" rating because everything about the novel, except its spine, seemed to be too thin. I guess I mean that several things happened so quickly that Koontz forgot to make any explanatory links between them. The novel felt very thrown together, as if maybe the author had promised to write something, but was very behind. Variations on the un</span>
  <span id="freeText5847798124709321968" style="display:none"><i>Velocity</i> certainly interested me enough to encourage quick reading, so the skeleton of the story can't be that bad. But I can only give it the two-star "it's okay" rating because everything about the novel, except its spine, seemed to be too thin. I guess I mean that several things happened so quickly that Koontz forgot to make any explanatory links between them. The novel felt very thrown together, as if maybe the author had promised to write something, but was very behind. Variations on the unbelievable, corny line--"How're they hangin', Kemosabe"?--were present not once, but four or five times. Far too much description littered the pages, things the reader has neither a need for nor an interest in. And the most interesting moments, the revelatory or exploratory ones, the ones dealing with the human condition and the hearts of men, were reduced to one or two short, ultimately inadequate sentences. Perhaps to add a little depth, Koontz relies on T.S. Eliot's words throughout <i>Velocity</i>, but the story does only a superficial job of providing them context. Read it for a laugh, read it to find out who the killer is. Read it because you're bored and have had enough television. Just don't be too sad when the climax doesn't manage to surprise. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5847798124709321968" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_478913964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478913964" />
    <a title="J.S. Bailey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5281321-j-s-bailey"><img alt="J.S. Bailey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570121244p2/5281321.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_416849208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/416849208" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2663305-james"><img alt="James" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/416849208?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/2663305-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007196975" href="/book/show/906900.Velocity">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416849208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5231757240609016837"><i>Velocity</i> is the first Dean Koontz novel that I have read, primarily because he writes in a genre I am not particularly fond of. Actually that’s not really true – I like a good thriller, but I am a pretty squeamish kind of guy, and Koontz (or so the book blurbs would imply) has a tendency to delve into the darker and more horrific sides of human nature. Having said that, I must admit I really enjoyed <i>Velocity</i>. I couldn’t put it down, turning the pages into the wee small hours of the morning.<br/><br/>Gener</span>
  <span id="freeText5231757240609016837" style="display:none"><i>Velocity</i> is the first Dean Koontz novel that I have read, primarily because he writes in a genre I am not particularly fond of. Actually that’s not really true – I like a good thriller, but I am a pretty squeamish kind of guy, and Koontz (or so the book blurbs would imply) has a tendency to delve into the darker and more horrific sides of human nature. Having said that, I must admit I really enjoyed <i>Velocity</i>. I couldn’t put it down, turning the pages into the wee small hours of the morning.<br /><br />Generally, I don’t like serial killer books. So with that knowledge you’re probably wondering why or how I came to read <i>Velocity</i> at all. It was pure chance. When buying another book, the store I was in was having a promotion – and I was able to select another book for free from a shelf in the store. This shelf was poorly stocked for male readers. There were quite a few ‘chic-lit’ novels, but about two that would appeal to guys like me – one of them was a reprint of <i>Casino Royale</i> – and those who know me, can be assured that I already have in excess of ten copies of CR, with various covers already scattered throughout the house. The other was <i>Velocity</i>.<br /><br />Apart from being a squeamish kind of guy - I dabble in graphic design, and as such, over the years have been known to comment on cover artwork, on things that ‘work’ and things that definitely ‘don’t work’. The thing here to remember is that ‘graphic design’ and ‘marketing’ are two very different disciplines, and while a book cover may be well designed, it does not necessarily follow that it reflects the nature of the story – or perhaps more importantly, sell copies of the book.<br /><br />The paperback edition of <i>Velocity</i> that I picked up (you can see the cover at the top of this post), is what I’d consider a lazy and messy design. But as a marketing tool, it is incredibly strong – but first to help explain what I mean, maybe it’s time I had a quick look at the story.<br /><br />The story concerns Billy Wiles who works as a bartender in the Napa Valley. Billy is an amiable enough guy, but over the years he has suffered a few hardships and setbacks. These days he keeps pretty much to himself. One evening, after finishing his shift at the bar, in the carpark, tucked under his windscreen wiper, he finds as note. Paraphrased it says:<br /><br />‘If you don’t take this note to the police, I will KILL a lovely blonde schoolteacher somewhere in Napa County<br /><br /><br />If you do take this note to the police, I will instead KILL an elderly woman.<br /><br />You have six hours to decide. The choice is yours’<br /><br />It’s a beautiful setup. Even by not acting, and ignoring the note, Billy is making a choice. He is a part of the game – with a madman – regardless if he likes it or not.<br /><br />But briefly, back to the cover art – the words from the note are depicted on the cover. Now graphically, it is not high art – it is quite messy. But from a marketing point of view, without having read a page, simply picking the book up, I really wanted to know which decision Billy was going to make and why? Simply, I had to buy this book. There were questions that needed to be answered.<br /><br />That note is really the whole setup to the story. Like it or not, Billy is drawn into a cat and mouse game against a serial killer who appears to know Billy’s moves one step before Billy even knows them.<br /><br />The central conceit of the book, to make the story work, is that Billy as a fourteen-year-old boy was seriously mistreated by the head police officer in Napa County, John Palmer. While Palmer is only in the story for a few pages, his spectral presence colours every move that Billy makes. Which sort of rules out the old ‘why don’t you just go to the police’ scenario. The thing here, is Koontz tells his story with such pace, while reading the story, you actually don’t question the logic and trust and go with the character of Billy.<br /><br />The story is very well written within the narrow scope that Koontz has chosen to place his story in. Everything is through Billy’s eyes, while this helps in understanding Billy’s perspective, it does leave the other characters motivations rather thin.<br /><br />It also hides the killer to the very end of the book, which works in the context of the story, but with barely any real interaction from the killer, the story lacks a certain menace. What I am clumsily alluding to is that the story lacks a villain that truly scares the pants of you. I know some people suggest that the ‘theatre of the mind’ is much scarier than what is shown or told, but I tend to believe that a hero is only as good as the villain that he is pitted against – and with the limited interaction between the main protagonists, the story does lack a certain edge.<br /><br />Having said all that – rather than a serial killer thriller chiller – as a fast paced, page turning psycho drama, Velocity is top-notch. Koontz sets up the boundaries and the stories conceits early, and then just runs with them for all they are worth, and the end result is damn readable – so much so, that despite my nature, I will make an effort to seek out and read more of his work. It ain’t high art – but on a cold winter’s night, it’s a good excuse to lie in bed with the doona pulled around you, and be transported to another place – just for a few hours (or if you’re like me, well into the morning).</span>
  <a data-text-id="5231757240609016837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15635547083999440722"><i> A man can be destroyed but not defeated. </i><br/> - Ernest Hemmingway, <i> The Old Man and The Sea</i><br/><br/>April 2016 Group Read in the Koontzland - Dean Koontz Group.<br/>March 2011 Group Read in the Koontzland - Dean Koontz Group. <br/><br/>This was the second Dean Koontz book that I read (after Watchers which unlike most people - didn't do it for me)- Velocity is the one that fish-hooked me and really nailed me down as a fan, even though the main character's actions drive me crazy!   <span id="freeText15635547083999440722" style="display:none"><i> A man can be destroyed but not defeated. </i><br /> - Ernest Hemmingway, <i> The Old Man and The Sea</i><br /><br />April 2016 Group Read in the Koontzland - Dean Koontz Group.<br />March 2011 Group Read in the Koontzland - Dean Koontz Group. <br /><br />This was the second Dean Koontz book that I read (after Watchers which unlike most people - didn't do it for me)- Velocity is the one that fish-hooked me and really nailed me down as a fan, even though the main character's actions drive me crazy! This is my fourth time reading Velocity :-)<br />Short chapters = a fast read.<br /><br />There is a lot of misperception in this novel:<br /><i>His age was difficult to determine. He might have been forty or sixty, but not thirty or seventy.<br /><br />Perhaps four minutes had passed since he'd hung up the phone after his conversation with Rosayln Chan. Maybe five. It felt like an hour; it felt like ten seconds. </i><br /><br />I do find the judgements of Billy against another main character rather disturbing. The entire book he is being judged and I would think maybe he just needs a chance. This character says "I know what I am, but I also know what I can be." I will admit to being rather infuriated. I don't believe misunderstood people are always evil. <br /><br />Favorite Passages:<br /><br /><i> "That's your world. It isn't mine."<br />"There's just one world."<br />"No, sir. There's a billion of them. Mine's different from yours, and that's the way it's gonna stay."<br />"We're sitting here on the same porch."<br />"No, sir. It looks like one porch, but it's two, all right. You know that's true. I see it in you."<br />"See what?"<br />"I see the way you're a little like me."<br />______<br /><br />....the freak possessed a knack for duplicity, a faculty for obfuscation, a talent for deception, and a genius for carefully crafted enigma. He preferred the oblique to the straightforward, the circuitous to the direct.<br />______<br /><br />With no corpse burrito in the Explorer, Billy risked exceeding the speed limit......<br />______<br /><br />"You're only thirty-four. From my perspective, you're barely past puberty."<br />"Mozart died younger than thirty-four."<br />"This isn't the eighteenth century, and you don't even play the piano," Harry said, "so the comparison makes no sense." He frowned "Are you sick or something?"<br />_______<br /><br />She vanished as completely as if she had stepped out of this universe into another.<br />_______<br /><br />She continued to meet his eyes. "Do you think every face is a mask, Billy?"<br />"Do you?"<br />"My deaf grandmother, as gentle and kind as any saint, still had her secrets. They were innocent, even charming secrets. Her mask was almost transparent as glass - but she still wore one."<br /><br /></i></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358600717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1898073219332841062">I like suspense and danger but not this type of suspense and danger.<br/><br/>I purchased this three years ago. I could not finish it. I did not do a review at the time thinking Koontz was not an author for me. Recently I read Lightning by Koontz and loved it. Therefore I’m now reading several of his books. I’m posting this as part of a group of reviews for comparison purposes - for readers who have tastes similar to mine.<br/><br/>I was frustrated, afraid, and felt hopeless watching Bill being threatened and manip</span>
  <span id="freeText1898073219332841062" style="display:none">I like suspense and danger but not this type of suspense and danger.<br /><br />I purchased this three years ago. I could not finish it. I did not do a review at the time thinking Koontz was not an author for me. Recently I read Lightning by Koontz and loved it. Therefore I’m now reading several of his books. I’m posting this as part of a group of reviews for comparison purposes - for readers who have tastes similar to mine.<br /><br />I was frustrated, afraid, and felt hopeless watching Bill being threatened and manipulated by the killer. Each time the killer killed someone he would plant murder evidence in Bill’s home or property. Bill had to frantically search, find, and get it out. I prefer the protagonist be able to have some control over something.<br /><br />My feeling: The killer is laughing as he forces a bug to run around in a maze, eventually planning to squish him. I am the bug. This was no fun. Maybe it was good at the end, but I couldn’t stand being in the maze long enough to get there.</span>

<div id="review_2868229565" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2868229565" />
    <a title="Ilia-Renee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51026929-ilia-renee"><img alt="Ilia-Renee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539567009p2/51026929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2868229565?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ilia-Renee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ilia-Renee" href="/user/show/51026929-ilia-renee">Ilia-Renee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2868229565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6531605347918423422">I own a few of Koontz books, but this is the first that I’ve read and wow! It was so good. So fast paced and kept me on the edge of my seat. I read a lot of thrillers, so I really look for things that are different. The killer in this book was doing things that I haven’t read in a book before. It was so sadistic and I loved it so much! </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_524515377" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/524515377" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11161028-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562512310p2/11161028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/524515377?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/11161028-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007196968" href="/book/show/1021397.Velocity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11161028-kim?shelf=oz-may-genre-2020">oz-may-genre-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer524515377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9194195675265611184">Billy Wiles is a barman in a small family bar in Vineyard Hills, California - he doesn't really do much with his life since his girlfriend fell into a coma through food poisoning some four years previously. At the time, he seemed destined to be a great writer but his drive and inspiration fell by the wayside with Barbara's accident. <br/>Then, leaving work one evening, Billy finds a note under his windscreen wiper saying that, if he doesn't take the note to the police and get them interested, the wri</span>
  <span id="freeText9194195675265611184" style="display:none">Billy Wiles is a barman in a small family bar in Vineyard Hills, California - he doesn't really do much with his life since his girlfriend fell into a coma through food poisoning some four years previously. At the time, he seemed destined to be a great writer but his drive and inspiration fell by the wayside with Barbara's accident. <br />Then, leaving work one evening, Billy finds a note under his windscreen wiper saying that, if he doesn't take the note to the police and get them interested, the writer of the note would kill a pretty blonde schoolteacher but if he did take the note to the police he would kill an elderly woman involved in charity work. Taking the note to his friend Lanny, a sheriff's deputy, it is dismissed as a prank, possibly by one of Billy's colleagues known for such tricks so nothing is done - and a blonde schoolteacher is killed. So begins a battle of wits between Billy and the mysterious killer, with Billy being presented with more bizarre 'choices'. Billy wonders what the killer is after and why he has been selected for the torturous game? But Billy is resourceful - he has learned to be after his experiences as a teenager - and plots to turn the tables on the mysterious killer, if he can only find out who he is!<br />A good read without being one of the author's best works, it was gripping enough although the characters were not particularly great so only rated this as 7/10.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9194195675265611184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_109861619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109861619" />
    <a title="Kasia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2087548-kasia"><img alt="Kasia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494441972p2/2087548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109861619?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kasia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kasia" href="/user/show/2087548-kasia">Kasia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109861619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17469077569831351084">Reading this book was quite fun, perhaps best described as feeling very lucky for not being in the main character's shoes. For a regular young guy keeping busy by bar tending, Billy Wiles is not very remarkable until we see him in distress. Out of the blue his life is being pulled in all sorts of crazy directions and the puppeteer pulling all his strings is a total freak who plays twisted mind games and plants all sorts of discriminating evidence in Billy's house, memorabilia of his past killing</span>
  <span id="freeText17469077569831351084" style="display:none">Reading this book was quite fun, perhaps best described as feeling very lucky for not being in the main character's shoes. For a regular young guy keeping busy by bar tending, Billy Wiles is not very remarkable until we see him in distress. Out of the blue his life is being pulled in all sorts of crazy directions and the puppeteer pulling all his strings is a total freak who plays twisted mind games and plants all sorts of discriminating evidence in Billy's house, memorabilia of his past killings in random bodies and parts planted to keep him from running to the police. When he starts finding random notes asking him who to spare and who to kill, Billy refuses to play the game, but his friends start disappearing and he has no choice but to play the game and maybe even try and win it, without turning into a psycho himself.<br /><br />I haven't read Koontz in a while, not by any conscious choice, but this week I suddenly craved his stable fiction that always satisfies, like a piece of cake, there are plenty of choices and they rarely fail even if they aren't the most nutritious. For some odd reason I couldn't get into the book at first, it reads fast but the first fifty pages were not a smooth read, perhaps I was being distracted by my surrounding but once I had time and quiet the book zoomed past me and I read it in two days. Most of the time at the end of each short chapter, the final paragraphs kept exploding with more and more crazy stuff, it felt like Billy was never getting his innocence and sanity back and it was impossible to put the book away or go to sleep or do anything else. The title defies the book perfectly, the way one person's life starts to crumble, the hole in the ground being dug deeper and deeper by a mysterious foe who knows everything about Billy but who's pulling the rug from under his feet in random directions getting him into more trouble by the minute. Playing tricks and games, treating people and their precious lives as a toy; something to play with, to get off to, the killer is cunning and cold, driving though his plan to bring Billy down. But lucky for us Billy is no sap and in some interesting ways plans to catch up to the maniac.<br /><br />Koontz does a great job of making Billy feel for all those who have perished, the deaths aren't meaningless and added to make the book soupy with gore, they are mourned and talked about form different angles, making the reader feel real sorrow and it made me think a little more about my own mortality, the way it can so easily be extinguished. Luckily this was just a book, and a great way to spend a dark and cold night. Now of course all I want to read is Koontz...I must say, he's a little bit addictive and I've acquired quite a bit of his stuff over the years. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17469077569831351084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kTVbDelsa/rTsm9GAADBNGAMiql/o0buCjB53iWwuXGZug8Rz6OA9eVlOlPgIISYcGT7GUcL68ueIhj9u/lntQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OtcPxZfbbhPcxrJwbgzYDtJyV20YJyc9bV2yLLoaqtoyWFvZsRSFHOoR52WOLJ2iwhom3SCPihj5T9MPJFN0Hg==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText12369192204397603602" style="display:none">Acknowledged as "America's most popular suspense novelist" (Rolling Stone) and as one of today's most celebrated and successful writers, Dean Ray Koontz has earned the devotion of millions of readers around the world and the praise of critics everywhere for tales of character, mystery, and adventure that strike to the core of what it means to be human.<br /><br />Dean, the author of many #1 New York Times bestsellers, lives in Southern California with his wife, Gerda, their golden retriever, Elsa, and the enduring spirit of their goldens, Trixie and Anna.<br /> <br />Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://Facebook.com/DeanKoontzOfficial">Facebook.com/DeanKoontzOfficial</a><br />Twitter: @DeanKoontz<br />Website: DeanKoontz.com </span>
